Free Talk

A Laughing Matter 105

— Sea Guest

Poor man (holding her leg and crying to a rich housewife)—Madam, your dog is too vicious. How can you let it bite people outside? It bit off a piece of meat from my leg.

Rich woman: Thank you for feeding him. It saves me a piece of beef to feed it. It's delicious to eat beef with green onions.

A: I'm marrying your sister this time. I'll be lonely at your house from now on. Will you hate me?

B: Everyone has a heart of compassion. We have no time to hate you, we pity you.

Husband: My dear, don't forbid me to smoke cigars. You should know that most of the great figures in the world smoke cigars. Wait until you become a great figure and then smoke. You are not allowed to smoke now.

Judge (asking a young woman who wants a divorce): Madam, how old are you this year?

Young woman: This year I am twenty-five years old. Judge: Huh? Why are you always twenty-five years old? I remember you said the same thing when you asked for a divorce the year before last.

Young woman: You should know that I am a person who doesn't like to talk nonsense at all. How I said it before is how I say it now.

Old gentleman: So, you want to be my son-in-law? Young man: I dare not, I dare not. But in order to marry your daughter, I have to reluctantly do so.

Postscript of Madame Chiang's Comfort Visit to the Front Lines 106

— Old Farmer Tian Yu

My friend Huang Junji Yan Yu has been in business in Guide for many years. Yesterday, he sent a letter describing in detail the victories of the national army and Madame Chiang Song Meiling's visit to the front lines to comfort the soldiers. I have specially recorded it in the Free Talk. (The following are all Huang Jun's descriptions in the letter)

After Madame Chiang Song Meiling set off from Xuzhou, she immediately telegraphed the temporary personnel and the key people of the front-line troops to wait for a welcome. When she arrived at the station in the evening, military music was melodious, and the welcomers bowed in salute. Madame smiled and thanked them one by one, and then walked to the camp (the camp was in the train). Commander-in-Chief Chiang Kai-shek was already standing next to the road under the poplar tree. Madame hurriedly stepped forward to shake hands and sat on the grass to inquire about the current military and national affairs and the progress plan, and reported the current situation of the National Government and the sincerity of comforting the front-line soldiers. Then she asked about Chiang's hard work in supervising the army and his health. Chiang said with a smile that he was very confident in the military progress and that the elimination of Yan Feng was just around the corner. As for his health, the environment was excellent and he felt more happy mentally. Although he only slept three or four hours a day, his appetite had increased greatly, which was comforting. Those who were sitting around were all solemn and respectful because Madame earnestly encouraged them with national affairs and did not mention personal matters. That night, they stayed in the camp train. The next morning, accompanied by the counselor, secretary, and guards, they went to the front line to inspect everything, inquire about the sufferings of the soldiers, and encourage them with great righteousness. Whenever there was an injured person, Madame would press the wound with her hand and ask about the circumstances when he was hit by the bullet, just like a loving mother treating an infant. She also advised the officers to love the soldiers and share their joys and sorrows. Then there was a thunderous cheer, and they were extremely grateful and vowed to die to repay Madame. Madame thanked them one by one, saying that when she returned in triumph in the future, she would personally celebrate with you all. She then inspected the trenches for a week and saw that the trenches were deep and wide, with electric nets and strict defenses, and the ammunition was abundant. She then said goodbye to the officers and returned to the camp. After talking with Chiang for a while, she took a special train back to Xuzhou and headed south. In recent days, the front-line progress has been rapid. It is said that the soldiers are grateful for Madame's kindness and are not afraid to sacrifice themselves and vow to die to repay her. If so, then Madame will be powerful when she returns in triumph in the future.

Strange Prophecy 107

— Nanqiang

The other residence of a certain Mr. in the west of Nanjing city has an area of more than ten acres. There is a pond in the center, which is as clear as a mirror. The surrounding pavilions and terraces are exquisitely structured. When the willow wind comes and the plum blossoms moon up, it is a natural painting. The owner is fond of elegance and has set up an incense community on the pond to worship the wandering immortals. Every morning and evening when the flowers bloom and the moon rises, he gathers famous people to practice divination and chanting. It is customary. My friend Liu Jun Hanbi and the owner are good friends. A month ago, he went to Ning for business and stayed in this garden. He was also invited to join the community. At that time, Chiang Kai-shek was supervising the army on the front line, and there were rumors that he was injured and various other unfavorable news. Liu Jun then asked the altar. The divination pen circled for a long time and then wrote three place names in the capital: Jiangshan (i.e., Zhongshan), Zhengzhong Street, and General An Lane, and then retreated. The crowd was puzzled. Later, after carefully examining the first characters of the names, they realized that it was Chiang Kai-shek An. In early May, Liu Jun returned to the old place and went to the altar to ask how the north and south would win or lose. The divination pen wrote three place names in the capital again: Jiangshan, Zhengzhong Street, Dashengguan, and then retreated, indicating the meaning of Chiang Kai-shek's great victory. In less than ten days, the prediction was fulfilled. Although the matter belongs to superstition and is not enough to be relied on, my friend said it was true and definitely not unfounded. I will just tell it casually, and you can listen to it casually.

On Leaving the Government 108

— Tao Zaidong

Since the Revolution of 1911, there have been many wars that have never been thoroughly resolved. It's just that one or two leaders leave the government. I, a foolish little Confucian scholar, do not know current affairs and dare not talk nonsense. Today, I will only study the two words "leaving the government" for the purpose of quibbling. According to the mountains and wilderness, the grass and wilderness are relative to the halls and pavilions of the imperial court. The term "leaving the government" is passed down from Japan. When the Emperor of that empire orders the cabinet to be formed, the cabinet ministers who leave their posts are called "leaving the government." It is justified. If our country only has the National Government, only government officials, and no cabinet to enter or court to go to, how can there be wilderness to leave? "Leaving the government," "leaving the government," people say it, and others also say it. It is not only ignorant but also violates the national system. It should be prohibited. If it is prohibited, there must be an appropriate term to replace it. I think that no term is more appropriate than "going to sea." Why is it true? Historically, those who leave the government all go abroad. Instead of twisting and turning to say going abroad, why not frankly call it "going to sea"? Or some people think that the two words "going to sea" are made up. According to my research, Cai Zhuangyuan repaired the Luoyang Bridge, and Xia Dehai made it into Xia Dehai. Therefore, this play is called "Going to Sea". Also, in "Dream of the Red Chamber", Miaoyu was robbed, and this group of robbers instead lit official lanterns and left the city to join the gang at sea. It can be proved that "going to sea" is not made up. Or some people think that actors and robbers are too undignified. According to my research, during the Shunzhi and Kangxi periods of the Qing Dynasty, when troops were used in Taiwan and Penghu, there was an edict that the people of the coastal areas of Fujian and Zhejiang should be moved inland, and fishing boats were not allowed to go to sea. It can be found in the court reports and strategic plans, which are more dignified than the words "leaving the government" under the teeth and spit. Furthermore, the rise and fall of the official sea is the most uncertain. For example, those who were called "leaving the government" in the past often moved for a while to revoke the wanted order and came to be officials again, but there was no appropriate term. Now, it is called "going to sea". If there is a former situation, it can be called "Shanghai" from the evolution of the official sea. There is a classic saying as evidence: "Spring and Autumn Classic, the Western Palace has a disaster." Gongyang Zhuan said: "If there is a Western Palace, then we know that there is an Eastern Palace." Now, according to its example, if there is "going to sea", then we know that there is "Shanghai" too. However, the words "up" and "down" here are verbs, not nouns. In other words, Shanghai is not a concession. Those who go abroad often do not go, or they sneak into the concession, so it is almost impossible to replace "going to sea" with "Shanghai" as a "leaving the government" theory.

Remembering John Bengtsson, Who Died in a Bicycle Accident 109

— Huang Yingdai

Bicycle racing has long been popular in Europe and the United States, but it has never been heard of in China. This time, since the opening of the Weile Garden, Chinese people have been able to see the art of bicycle racing. The news of the opening of Weile Garden has been repeatedly reported in various newspapers, but a tragic incident occurred before the opening. The details of the incident are believed to be known to readers, so there is no need to repeat them. However, there are few descriptions of the facts of the victim himself, so I will describe what I know.

John Bengtsson was the training director of Weile Garden bicycles and was from Sweden. He was 24 years old. He received higher education in Sweden. After graduating, he engaged in navigation. In 1924, he was transferred to the Shanghai Water Patrol Team and then entered the Shanghai Municipal Council. According to the Chinese in the Municipal Council, Bengtsson had no foreign temper at all. Usually, he treated colleagues in the bureau equally, regardless of their rank, and treated people with courtesy. Therefore, colleagues, regardless of Chinese or Western, were happy to associate with him. One day, the Western servant hired in his apartment suddenly suffered from an acute illness. Bengtsson personally took him to the hospital for treatment by car. When getting on and off the car, the patient was unable to move, and Bengtsson personally carried him into the car. This kind of philanthropy is really worthy of our imitation.

Bengtsson was usually known for his athletic skills. When he was in Europe, he won many championships, and his art of riding a bicycle was especially amazing. This time, Bengtsson was one of the initiators of the opening of Weile Garden. He resigned from his position in the Municipal Council before the event and worked day and night for several months to plan the layout of the venue and train the riders. Therefore, Bengtsson contributed half of the effort to the opening of Weile Garden. It was a pity that an unfortunate tragedy occurred a few days before the opening. One day, a Westerner in the venue who was good at driving a motor bicycle was practicing driving, and he was driving quite fast. Bengtsson couldn't help but want to show his skills, so he bravely boarded the car and sped around the venue, thinking of breaking his record. However, although Bengtsson was good at riding a bicycle, he lacked experience in riding a motor bicycle. When driving fast, he accidentally drove out of the track and fell off the road with the car and broke a leg. He was rushed to the hospital for treatment but eventually died. Those who heard about it all mourned and regretted it.

Good News for the People of Hangzhou 110

— Qiulang

The people take food as their heaven, so grains are indispensable to us every day. Only the people of Jiangnan eat rice, while the people of the north mostly eat wheat, which is slightly different. My relative, Mr. Wu, has just returned from Wulin and said that the price of rice in Hangzhou has plummeted, which is not without good news for the people's food. Therefore, I will briefly summarize the reasons for the sudden drop in rice prices, which I believe will also be welcome to those who care about the food issue.

According to various counties in Zhejiang Province, such as Zhu, Sheng, Chang, and Yu, they are originally abundant rice-producing areas. There is an old saying that "the fields in Zhu and Ji are ripe, and the whole world eats a bowl of porridge." However, in recent years, there have been years of poor harvests, coupled with good merchants smuggling and hoarding, which has led to a continuous increase in rice prices. It was previously heard that the price of rice in Shanghai was as high as tens of dollars per stone. Alas, the people really have the feeling of cooking with a few grains of rice. This year, the weather has been good, and the fields in Hangzhou and other counties have had bumper harvests. The villagers are all happy. Near the time of the autumn harvest, the farmers in the four villages have been transporting them to the province for sale, and the rice shops are filled with goods, and they cannot be completely accepted. However, the villagers are eager to sell their goods, so several rice merchants who have closed their businesses have seized the opportunity to raise funds to purchase them, and they also sell them at a lower price because the purchase price is low. When the rice shops saw this, they had to immediately cut prices in order to compete for business. It was heard that on the most violent day, the reduction was as much as two yuan. Now, the top rice is only sold for more than eleven yuan per stone. Vegetables, food, and other items have all fallen in price due to the decline in rice prices. This is indeed good news for the citizens of Hangzhou.

Nanyang Travel Notes (59) 111

— Linghua

May 27th, a report said that French Academy scholar J. Barthelemp's new school of law advocated leaning towards dictatorship and not focusing on the masses. I have not read the content of his thesis, but based on my years of research, I use the Chinese Doctrine of the Mean to evaluate the facts, and I believe that focusing on dictatorship and focusing on the masses are both biased views. French people recently felt the dictatorship of Russia on the one hand and the dictatorship of Mussolini in Italy on the other. Dictatorship can make the national strength strong, so jurists also advocate dictatorship, but not focusing on the masses in fact has long lost the Doctrine of the Mean. To solve human problems, wisdom, benevolence, and courage are indispensable. If you want to solve problems in electrochemistry, you must be a person who understands electrochemistry. If millions of laymen gather and vote on it, none of them will be correct. In the past, we relied solely on autocracy, and today we move with the roar of the masses. The former way is to bully the weak, and the current way is to use the majority to oppress the minority, which is not the Doctrine of the Mean. My research results show that human nature does not have equality for one day, so it is only possible to do as Mozi said: "How to be a virtuous person? Those who have strength should quickly help others, those who have wealth should strive to share with others, and those who have morality should diligently teach others. If so, the hungry will get food, the cold will get clothes, and the chaos will be governed." (Shangxianxia) Therefore, it must be guided by the wise and knowledgeable before it can be brought into the right track. The Republic of Socrates in ancient times advocated the system of virtuous people, so he was opposed by Anytus and Meletus, who advocated the system of the masses at that time, and was killed, and Socrates' death was decided by a vote of five hundred people. Recently, Spanish philosopher George Santayana 1 3—compared the results of all academic studies and still advocated that the Republic of Socrates may be a system of open access for all classes of men and women, but it must use culture and knowledge, not blindly follow the majority, because the emotions and knowledge of the masses are difficult to rely on. Because numbers cannot produce true right and wrong, world revolutions and extraordinary great causes are mostly created by the unique knowledge of those who leave the number and act alone. However, its plan must be beneficial to the masses. China has followed the ancient Tao of Yao and Shun, which is to advocate virtuous governance and not value autocracy.

May 28th, the Guanghua Daily here suddenly received a government order to suspend publication for three months, which was said to be due to the May Day labor holiday text. A few days ago, the Singapore Republic Daily was also suspended for two months by the government's order because the Japanese consul protested to the British government for publishing the Jinan Massacre. During the suspension period, it was heard that all expenses were still not saved, and the penalty was not small. There are four newspapers here, and Guanghua is the leading one. There is also an English weekly. There are six newspapers in Singapore. Dongshi Communication (19) 112

— Wu Xiaohou

Shiba Park. Shiba Park is named because it is located in the Shiba district. In the beginning, most of it was the site of the Zojoji Temple on Mt. Sanyuan. In the sixth year of Meiji, according to the announcement of the Grand Council, Ueno, Asakusa, etc. were changed into parks. Half of the park is the plateau of Akasaka and Azabu. The terrain of Shibaura in the east is extremely low, and this park is located at the protruding end. The undulating hills and old trees are verdant and lush. The total head temple of the Kanto Jodo sect, Zojoji Temple, is located in the center of the park, which is the mausoleum of the Tokugawa family and the Toshogu Shrine. There is a main road running north and south from Omon to Shibaen Bridge. To the east of it are temples and residential areas with park facilities. Electric trains pass through it. Other major roads lead from Omon up Ginkgo Slope, pass in front of the Red Leaf Waterfall, and pass through the Zhaobian Tiantou pond and circle around the roads inside Shibaen Bridge and under the Maruyama and in front of the mountain gate. The main road in the park is divided into twenty-five districts, with the center point of Zojoji Temple and Orei Hall as the first district. To the west of it is a gourd-shaped large ancient tomb, famous for its five-storied pagoda and Maruyama old cedar pavilion, which stand covering the sky and the sun. It is truly a natural forest park. To the south of Maruyama is Toshogu Shrine. There is a large ginkgo tree twenty-one feet high. The plum grove continues to the shrine and autumn grass is planted along the roadside. From the bottom of Maruyama to the south to the Old River, there is a large sports field with a width of 4,000 tsubo. Black pine trees are planted on the mounds along the Old River to create a Japanese garden scene and form a series of hills. To the west of the field is a plum grove, which is called the Silver World. To the west of the grove is Myoteiin. The entrance between the courtyard and the Akahane Bridge is a sports field equipped with various sports equipment. There is a Benten Pond in the depression under the northwest cliff of Maruyama, which is truly a secluded scenic spot. There is an elegant natural stream flowing downstream under the pond, which surrounds the foot of Maruyama and reaches the side of Toshogu Shrine. To the west of the pond is a main road leading directly to Iikura. There is a large azalea garden between the banks of the stream, and the banks are lined with evergreen trees, so the sun cannot be seen during the day, which is very secluded. There is a waterfall on the cliff, so it is commonly called Red Leaf Waterfall. Near the waterfall is a small fairyland. The end of the stream is long and thin, irrigating Benten Pond. The slope to the west of the waterfall is called Red Leaf Slope. Climbing up, there is Sanrokudo, originally the site of the Noh theater. To the west of it is the famous Kondi-in. During the Tokugawa era, it was the office of the head of the green company, and Monk Honko (Soden) moved here from Edo Castle. The area near it is called Red Leaf Mountain, because there are many maple trees on the mountain. From the Red Leaf Hall, the valley roads along the Iikura area are lined with old trees, which are very reminiscent of deep mountains and valleys. Along this road is a small forest spring, which was formerly the garden of Rurikoji Temple. It has recently been purchased as a park. If you reach the highlands of No. 25 in the north, you can see most of the city. The area from Ginkgo Slope to Omon is called Matsubara Region. Square old pine forests stand, and the same is true in front of the mountain gate. It reaches Shibaen Bridge and points at the pines to accumulate fresh air. Central history and natural scenery are the true natural forest park. After visiting the park, Mr. Uchida and Ms. Shakae with whom I went together, took an automatic camera and took a photo together in front of the fountain in the park to commemorate it.

Financial and Gold Market Trends Are Sensitive and Active 113

The trend seems to be forward-moving. Yesterday, the 24th, the gold market seemed to show a solid interest, with the intention to increase. However, there were fluctuations of two taels at times. Throughout the day, there were differences totaling more than five taels, but ultimately, an upward trend was seen and the market was sensitive and active. As for foreign exchange, the trend was firm. There was no lack of interbank trading, with buyers being the majority. Yuanxing, Yongyuan, Yuancheng, Yongyu, Dada, Decheng, etc., had unsettled receipts and payments. Yuanmao, Yongzhi, and Fengyong sold items for hedging, while Taikangrun, Hanheng, etc., mostly bought in. From the early market, the opening was high, breaking through the 40-tael mark, as it was rumored that Japan had shipped cash to Citibank. Upon hearing this news, those in the industry were excited. Later, due to the active selling, there was a brief softening, but the buyers were persistent, and those covering short positions also came in droves, causing a sudden jump of more than four taels. In addition, drafts became increasingly tight. Later, the market strengthened and then weakened, with a fluctuation of about three taels, likely because Yuanmao, Yong, etc., turned from buying to selling, which caused some confusion in the market. However, due to it being Wednesday, there was no market for drafts. The final gold price was 43 taels.

The morning market fluctuated. In November, the opening price in the morning rose by 2 taels and 1 mace to 542 taels. Large bars were not improved, as there was talk that Japan was planning to ship cash to Citibank, which caused the market to rise. Later, there was a fluctuation of more than one tael, reaching over 40 taels and 6-7 mace. Local News

City Government Organizes Relief for Liaoxi Flood Yesterday 187

Temporary Change to Discussion Meeting

Successful and Joyful Conclusion

The Shanghai Municipal Government, deeply concerned about the severity of the Liaoxi flood and the urgent need for relief, convened representatives from various sectors of the city to discuss relief measures and organized a fundraising committee to actively carry out the work, as reported previously. It is now learned that the Municipal Government invited leaders from various Party, government, commercial, and community organizations in the city to a discussion meeting at the Atlantic Restaurant on Sima Road at 6:00 PM yesterday to discuss relief efforts. Over three hundred people attended, including Yu Qiaqing, Wang Xiaolai, and Wang Yiting. The details of the meeting are recorded below:

Change to Discussion Meeting: The Municipal Government originally intended to hold a banquet at the Atlantic Restaurant when sending out invitations the day before. However, due to a central government order to suspend entertainment banquets for three days following the death of Acting Chairman of the National Government, Tan Yankai, the event was temporarily changed to a discussion meeting. A letter was sent to community leaders stating: "Regarding the relief efforts for the Liaoxi flood, we previously sent an invitation to you to attend a meeting at the Atlantic Restaurant on the 24th of this month at 6:00 PM to discuss implementation methods. However, due to the death of Acting Chairman of the National Government, Tan Yankai, we have been ordered to suspend entertainment banquets for three days. As the matter concerns disaster relief, it is inconvenient to postpone the event, so we have changed it to a discussion meeting at the same location. Your presence is requested."

Chairman's Report: After the meeting commenced, Municipal Government Secretary-General Yu Hongjun reported on the purpose of the meeting, stating: "Gentlemen, Mayor Zhang has asked me to invite you here today to discuss relief measures for the Northeast flood. We are honored that you have accepted the invitation. Mayor Zhang himself is in Shenyang and unable to return to Shanghai, so he has asked me to represent him. I will briefly report on the situation of the Liaoxi flood. As you have likely seen in the newspapers, the affected area spans approximately six to seven hundred li wide and two to three hundred li long. The death toll is already five to six thousand, and hundreds of thousands are homeless. The weather is getting colder, and the disaster victims are suffering greatly. As winter approaches, their suffering will be even more unbearable. Mayor Zhang, having witnessed the situation in Shenyang firsthand, is deeply saddened and has repeatedly instructed us to request your enthusiastic support for relief efforts. Shanghai has always been known for its generosity and has never lagged behind in providing relief to disaster areas, earning the admiration of other regions and bringing glory to our city. The Liaoxi flood is exceptionally severe, and we must uphold the principle of benevolence and actively strive to be the first to help. I have previously met with community leaders at the Gongyu Club and decided to organize a Northeast Flood Relief Committee to actively carry out the work. However, the success of this effort depends on the collective strength of everyone. We hope that you will contribute generously and provide ample guidance so that the hundreds of thousands of starving disaster victims can be quickly relieved of their suffering. This is not only what Mayor Zhang hopes for, but also what the entire population of Shanghai hopes for."

Guest Speeches: Ye Huijun spoke next, stating: "Today, Mayor Zhang entrusted Secretary-General Yu to invite everyone here to discuss relief measures for the Liaoxi flood. Based on my understanding of the suffering of the Liaoxi disaster victims, the citizens of Shanghai should work together and contribute generously." Wang Xiaolai then spoke, stating: "Secretary-General Yu has clearly explained the purpose of this gathering tonight. Shanghai is much more comfortable than other places, so we should make even greater efforts to provide relief to the Northeast flood. Shanghai is a model for the whole country. In the past, whenever there was a disaster anywhere, we were always the first to provide relief. We hope that everyone will be charitable and contribute generously to this Liaoxi flood. As for fundraising methods, we can hold variety shows or direct fundraising." Zhang Xiaolin spoke next, stating: "Today, as we discuss fundraising methods, I have four suggestions: First, we can raise funds through opera performances, with Mr. Wang Xiaolai and Mr. Du Yuesheng in charge. Second, we can have dances, with Ms. Zheng Yuxiu in charge. Third, we can organize games and activities, and I suggest the Municipal Government contact them. Fourth, we can have on-the-spot donations. I hope that everyone will discuss these four methods." Xu Shiying then spoke, stating: "The Liaoxi flood is extremely serious. The chairman and Mr. Zhang have all mentioned several fundraising methods. I am the chairman of the Relief Committee, and today I would like to say a few words in my personal capacity. In the past, Shanghai has always been the most generous in providing relief donations to various provinces. I strongly support everyone's enthusiasm in fundraising and proposing various methods, and I hope that everyone present will make on-the-spot pledges, whether it is one dollar, one thousand, or ten thousand dollars. In short, every extra dollar donated will benefit the disaster victims." Yu Qiaqing spoke next, stating: "I deeply agree with Mr. Xu Shiying's remarks. The disaster victims in the Northeast are displaced and suffering, and they are in urgent need of rescue. Moreover, the Northeast authorities are doing their best to support the central government, making the central government more stable and ensuring the security of the rear. All of us in the rear should emulate the Northeast authorities' dedication to saving the country and the people and contribute as much as we can to alleviate the suffering of the Northeast disaster victims. The government has already prepared 200,000 yuan. If Shanghai can raise a considerable amount, then many more disaster victims in the Northeast will be saved. I hope that everyone present will donate as they see fit, the more the better."

On-the-Spot Donations: Community leaders expressed their strong support for on-the-spot donations and immediately made pledges. The Municipal Government pledged 10,000 yuan, and various organizations and leaders pledged a total of more than 16,500 yuan, totaling more than 26,500 yuan.

Successful Conclusion: After community leaders and merchants made their pledges, the results were deemed very satisfactory, and everyone dispersed happily. It was already past 9:00 PM.

Tang Shaoyi Comes to Shanghai on a Mission 188

To Discuss Matters Related to Zhongshan Port

Dalu Bao reported that Tang Shaoyi, a senior advisor to the National Government, returned to Shanghai a few days ago after spending three months in Guangdong. When a reporter visited Mr. Tang yesterday, he said that the rumors circulating that the Northern faction had sent someone to contact him to form a government were completely unfounded. He had not even heard of these rumors until he arrived in Hong Kong on this trip to Shanghai. He immediately issued a statement to foreign newspapers to clarify the matter. The main purpose of his return to Shanghai was to discuss the construction of Zhongshan Port with the central government. The construction of the port is currently progressing rapidly, but due to the scale of the project, it cannot be completed in a short time. The port will be a free trade port for the next sixty years, but it will not affect Hong Kong. Hong Kong's foundation is solid, and it has a good government to administer it. He believes that the opening of Zhongshan Port may actually make Hong Kong and Guangzhou more prosperous. He will go to Nanjing soon to discuss port affairs with government officials. When asked if he intends to accept the invitation from US President Hoover to visit the United States after he took office, Mr. Tang replied that he would very much like to have the opportunity to reminisce with President Hoover. He may be able to give a definite answer on this matter after his trip to Nanjing.

Li Gong Replies to Visiting Consuls 189

Liu Yunfang Accompanied Him Yesterday

Since taking office, Li Zhonggong, a commissioner of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, has been visited by consuls from various countries stationed in Shanghai. Yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM, Mr. Li, accompanied by Liu Yunfang, deputy director of the Foreign Affairs Office, visited British Consul-General Sir John Brenan. At 3:30 PM, he visited American Consul-General Mr. Cunninghan, and at 4:00 PM, he visited Japanese Acting Minister Mr. Shigemitsu Mamoru. The consuls warmly received them, and the discussions were very pleasant.

County Magistrate Yan Invites Township Heads to a Discussion 190

To Promote Local Self-Governance

County Magistrate Yan of Shanghai County believes that the establishment of townships is extremely important for the promotion of self-governance. Therefore, he has scheduled a meeting at 10:30 AM on the 30th of this month (Tuesday) in Chenxing, the fifth district of Pudong, to convene all township heads and deputies in the district to discuss the matter. A letter has been sent to each of them to attend.

Chinese and Foreign Communities Mourn President Tan 191

Navy: The local Navy ordered all ships to fly flags at half-mast to mourn the death of President Tan. The Navy Special Party Department also sent a telegram to Nanjing to express condolences, stating: "To the Funeral Committee for President Tan in Nanjing: We were shocked to learn of the sudden passing of President Tan and are deeply saddened. The Party and the country relied heavily on him, but unexpectedly, he lost his life. Heaven does not favor us, and the people have lost their teacher and protector. We send our condolences with deep respect."

Polish Minister: The Polish Charge d'Affaires to China, Mr. Weydenthal, accompanied by Counselor Mr. Goliginski, wore mourning attire and visited the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs at 12:00 noon yesterday to express his condolences on behalf of the Polish government.

Zhou and Ding: Zhou Qigang and Ding Chaowu, upon hearing the news of President Tan's death, decided to take the special express train to Nanjing at 9:00 AM today to express their condolences.

Canada Increases Import Tariffs 192

Chinese Businesses to be Hit Again

According to news from the shipping industry yesterday, the Canadian government has decided to increase import taxes on duty-free or lightly taxed goods in order to cope with recent economic policies. In particular, taxes on textiles and steel products will be increased significantly. China's export trade to Canada has been developing recently, and this move will have a significant impact. It is also reported that the Canadian government has submitted the new tax regulations to Congress for approval and will implement them soon.

US Commercial Attaché Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday 193

Visits Director Chen and Director Liu

Mr. Julean Arnold, the US Commercial Attaché to China, recently arrived in Shanghai from Beijing with Deputy Attaché Mr. Gold. Yesterday morning at 11:00 AM, they visited Director Chen Shiguang and Director Liu Yunfang at the Ministry of Foreign Affairs on Fenglin Bridge and consulted on commercial matters.

Xiangtai and Jiangxin Collide at Wusong Port 194

Both Ships Damaged

Xiangtai Already in Dock

The Jiangxin, a Yangtze River ship belonging to the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, was damaged when it collided with the British ship Xiangtai while transporting goods from Shanghai to Hankou at Wusong Port. The bow of the Xiangtai was severely damaged. Details of the incident are as follows:

Collision Details: The Jiangxin of China Merchants Steam Navigation Company left Shanghai on the morning of the 23rd and was sailing towards Wusong Port at about 9:00 AM, following the shipping channel. The Xiangtai, a Yangtze River ship of the Xiangtai Shipping Company, was sailing downstream from Hankou to Shanghai. The two ships met inside Wusong Port, heading in the same direction. At that time, the morning tide was rising, and the current was rapid. The crew of the Jiangxin saw the Xiangtai heading straight towards the left side. Unexpectedly, the current was strong, and the Xiangtai collided head-on with the Jiangxin in an instant. The Jiangxin immediately reversed, narrowly avoiding a head-on collision, but the right side of the hull was struck by the bow of the Xiangtai, damaging the iron plates and the hull.

Damage Condition: The Jiangxin is larger than the Xiangtai, and its steel plates are also stronger. When the Xiangtai struck, the Jiangxin managed to reverse, so the damage to the outside of the hull was above the waterline and did not affect navigation. When the Xiangtai collided with the Jiangxin, it could not stop due to the strong tide. The shipmaster, Mr. Richee, also reversed, but could not avoid the collision. Both ships were heavily loaded. The bow of the Xiangtai was severely damaged, and the iron plates were broken, making it impossible to navigate. Fortunately, the passengers and crew were already up, so no one was injured. Afterwards, the Xiangtai was towed to the dock, and the Jiangxin left Shanghai.

Repair News: The Jiangxin's schedule was tight, and the damage was above the waterline, so it continued to Hankou. The damaged part was repaired by the crew en route. It will be inspected and repaired further when it returns to Shanghai. The Xiangtai was towed to the dock, and the goods were unloaded. The shipmaster reported the damage to the customs and Shanghai authorities. The bow was severely damaged, and it was towed to the Ruirong Shipyard yesterday at noon for major repairs. The responsibility for the collision will be determined after an on-site investigation by both parties.

News from the Shipping Industry 195

Approval Fee to Increase: The Jianghai Customs has increased the application fee for import and export cargo loading and unloading night work by 80% at the request of various shipping companies. Shanghai shipping merchants held two public consultations and jointly requested the Tax Bureau to consider the difficulties of the shipping merchants and waive the increase. The Tax Bureau rejected the request. The previous day, another letter was sent appealing the decision. Yesterday, it was learned that the Customs had replied that the approval fee was set 50 years ago, and now that material costs have increased, it is not possible to maintain the original tax rate. The approved 80% increase will be implemented from August 16th. The request for exemption was rejected.

Straw Hat Fee Ordered to be Reduced: The Lian'an Shipping Company on the Shanghai-Taiwan route increased the freight rate for straw hats from the three counties of Linhai, Zhejiang. Wang Chongde, a representative of the industry's labor union, appealed to the Ministry of Communications to stop this practice, stating that the company controlled customs and shipping and repeatedly increased the straw hat freight rate from one li to eight li. Straw hats are one of the country's export goods, which is contrary to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce's policy of encouraging industry, providing financial assistance, and facilitating transportation. The Ministry of Communications has ordered the company to reduce the freight rate immediately to avoid monopolizing shipping.

Singaporean Organizations Petition for Lower Postal Rates for Overseas Chinese Letters 196

Overseas Chinese Federation Will Join Forces to Appeal Again

The Overseas Chinese Federation of the Republic of China received a petition from various Singaporean organizations to reduce postal rates for overseas Chinese letters. A letter from Lin Jindian, chairman of the delegation representing the Singaporean Overseas Chinese Congress, states: "To the Overseas Chinese Federation: Our association has submitted a document to the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission, the Executive Yuan, and the Ministry of Communications, requesting that they approve the previous request to establish special regulations based on international postal treaties to maintain the overseas Chinese practice of sending remittances and letters. The overseas Chinese postal service is crucial to the livelihood of overseas Chinese families. We have repeatedly appealed over the years, and while we are grateful for the understanding shown in reducing postal rates and revoking the suppression order, the request to establish special regulations with the British postal service has not been approved. Last month, we received a reply from the Ministry of Communications stating that the Postal Administration believed that special regulations were not necessary and might cause disputes that would be detrimental to the private postal service. Moreover, the existence of private postal services in our country makes it appear that our postal system is not unified, which is inconvenient in the international arena. The Nanyang Islands are British and Dutch territories, not independent countries, so rejection would be detrimental to the national image. Therefore, it is appropriate not to propose special regulations. We were shocked and worried to hear this. We do not know on what basis the Postal Administration made these claims. We convened a meeting to discuss the matter in detail. Everyone believes that the Ministry of Communications understands the hardships of overseas Chinese and cares for them greatly. However, the Ministry has instructed that the Postal Administration's proposal be followed, rejecting the overseas Chinese request, which is regrettable. We believe that the Postal Administration may not have international common sense or may be disregarding the overseas Chinese. We will rebut the Postal Administration's claims to the Ministry of Communications: (1) Private postal services at home and abroad were established for overseas Chinese to send remittances and letters to support their families. The matter is of utmost importance. Over the years, the Chinese government and local governments have issued suppression orders. The overseas Chinese have appealed and requested the preservation of the service, and then requested a reduction in rates. To permanently protect the service and provide a thorough solution, we requested the establishment of special regulations. However, the Postal Administration believes that special regulations are not necessary. We do not know the reason for this. If the British government resumes its suppression, how can we reject it? This is incomprehensible. (2) Negotiating special regulations is to avoid suppression and eliminate disputes, which is essential for the protection of the private postal service. However, the Postal Administration reverses the argument, saying that special regulations might cause disputes that would be detrimental to the private postal service. This is an unimaginable statement that leaves overseas Chinese in a state of confusion. Will special regulations cause disputes and be detrimental? What kind of disputes and what kind of harm will be caused? This is not clearly explained to us, and this is also incomprehensible. (3) The Postal Administration states that the Nanyang Islands are British and Dutch territories, not independent countries, so rejection would be detrimental to the national image. Therefore, it is appropriate not to propose special regulations. If so, if overseas Chinese in other regions encounter other major events, the Chinese government will also use the same excuse that the region is not an independent country, rejection would be detrimental to the national image, and allow overseas Chinese to be trampled on and abused. This will leave overseas Chinese in Nanyang without any protection. It is painful to say and brings tears to think about. This is also incomprehensible. Negotiating special regulations is based on the international postal treaty. Postal treaty countries have the right to negotiate with each other. Why would it be rejected? Moreover, we have not yet proposed it, so how do we know that the other party will reject it? Furthermore, last year, when negotiating with the British postal service about increasing postal rates, why was the issue of independent countries not considered? Why was there no fear of rejection? Why was the national image not considered? Is it because tax revenue is more important? The Singaporean private postal service has been operating for 70 or 80 years. The local government issued a license and approved its operation, which is a confirmation of its existence. The recent approval of the request to reduce postal rates was automatic, without the need to seek the opinion of international postal treaty countries, and there were no restrictions on the type of case. This clearly shows that the processing of individual special postal items between Nanyang and our country does not violate the international postal treaty and is not subject to interference by international postal treaty countries. To maintain the livelihood of families, special regulations are essential to prevent suppression of the private postal service. Therefore, we have unanimously decided to appeal again, earnestly requesting that the Postal Administration be instructed to negotiate special regulations with the British government to maintain the overseas Chinese practice of sending letters and remittances to support their families. We urgently await your reply. When private letters arrive in Xiamen and are transferred to the interior, and when return letters are sent from the interior to Xiamen, the Xiamen Post Office still requires additional postage stamps. We previously requested that this be cancelled, but it was not approved. We have decided to allow letters to be taken to the Xiamen Post Office and other inland post offices for inspection and stamping, and then resealed and delivered by the post office to avoid smuggling. We urgently request that you approve this request and cancel the additional postage to alleviate the hardship of overseas Chinese." The petition from the Singaporean organizations requesting a reduction in postal rates for overseas Chinese letters was submitted by Lin Jindian, chairman of the delegation representing the Singaporean Overseas Chinese Congress. The Overseas Chinese Federation believes that it is their responsibility to appeal again to the transportation authorities to approve the request of the overseas Chinese Congress to facilitate the sending of remittances and letters by overseas Chinese and to maintain the livelihood of millions of overseas Chinese families.

City Government Distributes Regulations on Customs Tax Bonds 197

Citizens Can Request Copies from Various Tax Collection Offices

The Municipal Government was ordered to raise 1 million yuan in customs tax bonds for the 19th year. A method of collecting them through housing rent has been decided, and various tax collection offices have been assigned to start collecting them within a specified time. The Municipal Government is deeply concerned that citizens may not be familiar with the regulations on customs tax bonds for the 19th year, as well as the repayment of principal and interest. Therefore, it has printed several copies of the "Regulations on Customs Tax Bonds for the 19th Year" based on the regulations issued by the central government and distributed them to various tax collection offices so that citizens can request them.

Two Regulations on the Management of Weights and Measures in This City 198

Regulations of the Shanghai Municipal Weights and Measures Verification Office

Operating Rules for Managing Weights and Measures Instruments

The Shanghai Municipal Government announced the Regulations of the Shanghai Municipal Weights and Measures Verification Office and the Operating Rules for Managing Weights and Measures Instruments yesterday. We have compiled them together below:

Regulations of the Shanghai Municipal Weights and Measures Verification Office: Article 1: This office is subordinate to the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau. Article 2: The functions of this office are as follows: (1) Verification and inspection of public and civil weights and measures instruments within the city. (2) Custody of secondary standards and prototypes issued by the Ministry and specimens. (3) Promotion of the new system. (4) Business registration of weights and measures instruments. (5) Guidance on the manufacture of new instruments and the improvement of old instruments. (6) Training of third-class verifiers. (7) Planning and supervision of branch offices. (8) Other administrative matters related to weights and measures. Article 3: This office shall have a director, several verifiers, and clerks. Employees may be hired when necessary. Article 4: The director, who is also the chief verifier, is responsible for all affairs of the office under the direction of the Social Affairs Bureau. The verifiers are responsible for verification, inspection, custody, promotion, guidance, and training under the direction of the director. The clerks handle documents, accounting, and general affairs. Article 5: The appointment, reward, and punishment of the director and verifiers shall be handled in accordance with the regulations for the use of weights and measures verification personnel. The clerks shall be appointed by the Social Affairs Bureau upon the recommendation of the director. Article 6: This office may establish departments to handle matters based on the nature of its functions. The detailed rules for handling matters shall be established separately. Article 7: The working conditions and expenditures of this office shall be reported to the Social Affairs Bureau for evaluation on a monthly basis and reported to the National Bureau of Weights and Measures of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for record. Article 8: These regulations may be amended at any time if there are any incomplete matters. Article 9: These regulations shall be implemented from the date of announcement by the Municipal Government.

Operating Rules for Managing Weights and Measures Instruments: Article 1: All factories that manufacture, repair, or sell weights and measures instruments within this city shall comply with the provisions of these rules. Article 2: Those who operate a business that manufactures, repairs, or sells weights and measures instruments shall first request registration with the Shanghai Municipal Weights and Measures Verification Office (hereinafter referred to as the Verification Office). Article 3: The procedures for registering a weights and measures instrument business are as follows: (1) Apply for a registration form. (2) The registration form shall be filled out in detail and submitted to the Verification Office with a trademark sample for inspection and approval. (3) If the inspection is unqualified, the applicant shall follow the instructions of the Verification Office to correct the defects and submit the form for re-inspection and approval. Article 4: The applicant shall obtain a business license from the Verification Office after receiving the notification of approval of registration and pay the license fee in accordance with Articles 3 and 4 of the Regulations on the Management of Weights and Measures Instruments. Article 5: If a weights and measures instrument business ceases operation within this city, the license shall be returned to the Verification Office regardless of whether it has expired. However, the license fee will not be refunded. Article 6: The business license for weights and measures instruments shall be displayed in a conspicuous place. If it is lost or damaged, it shall be reported in the newspaper and to the Verification Office for replacement. A replacement fee of two yuan shall be paid. Article 7: The business license for weights and measures instruments shall not be transferred to others for use. Article 8: When a weights and measures instrument business obtains a business license and commences operation, it shall comply with the provisions of the Detailed Rules for the Implementation of Weights and Measures and the Regulations on the Management of Weights and Measures Instruments. Article 9: The weights and measures instruments to be verified shall pay the verification fee in accordance with the Regulations on the Collection of Verification Fees for Weights and Measures Instruments. Article 10: Weights and measures instrument businesses shall be subject to regular or temporary inspections by the Weights and Measures Verification Office and shall not refuse. Article 11: Weights and measures instrument businesses shall report the prices and quantities of goods sold once a month and shall not conceal them. If there is any hoarding or manipulation, the Weights and Measures Verification Office may impose restrictions at any time. Article 12: These rules may be amended at any time if there are any incomplete matters. Article 13: These rules shall be implemented from the date of announcement by the Municipal Government.

More Chinese Laborers Sent Back from Japan 202

This newspaper has repeatedly reported on Japan's refusal to allow Chinese people to enter. Due to the contraction of various factories in Japan this year, over five hundred Chinese laborers who were working in Japan have been laid off and sent back to China in succession. Recently, forty-five Chinese workers from Yokohama, Japan, all from WenZhou and Qingtian counties in Zhejiang province, were also dismissed and unable to make a living in Japan. They were repatriated to Shanghai by the Japanese authorities and are now in a very distressed state. After arriving in Shanghai, some of these laborers have returned to their hometowns, while the rest, lacking a livelihood, are staying in small inns in the Nanshi area. In addition, more than ten Chinese people from the Kobe area have also been expelled and sent back to China.

City Federation of Trade Unions Requests Revocation of Notice No. 146 of the Social Affairs Bureau 204

Approved by the People’s Training Committee for Submission to the Central Government

Five Representatives Went to Nanjing to Petition Last Night

The Shanghai Tea Industry Trade Union, Calligraphy Trade Union, Pharmacy Trade Union, Pharmaceutical Industry Trade Union, Silk and Cloth Dyeing Industry Trade Union, Sauce Industry Trade Union, Dried Goods Trade Union, and over forty other trade unions, submitted a joint petition to the People’s Training Committee, requesting the revocation of Notice No. 146 of the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, which concerned the hiring and firing of shop assistants. The notice stipulated that commercial and industrial employers could temporarily follow the old customs of each industry. The trade unions believed that this notice would cause major disputes between labor and management. Yesterday, they received an instruction from the People’s Training Committee, stating: "The petition from the Tea Industry Trade Union, etc., regarding the request to revoke Notice No. 146 of the Social Affairs Bureau has been received. After investigation, the points raised by the trade union are indeed of deep concern. However, the said notice of the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau was issued under the order of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce. If it needs to be revoked or amended, the Ministry should order the Bureau to comply in order to conform to the administrative system. In addition to submitting this to the Central Government to request the National Government’s Ministry of Industry and Commerce to investigate and handle it, this is hereby notified."

Regarding Notice No. 146 of the Social Affairs Bureau, the trade unions held a meeting some days ago to discuss countermeasures. As a result, it was decided to send five representatives to Nanjing to petition. These representatives included Zhao Zhenhui from the Pharmaceutical Industry Trade Union, Hu Shouqi from the Calligraphy and Painting Trade Union, Sang Yutang from the Pharmacy Trade Union, Zhu Xiaoyun from the Silk and Cloth Dyeing Industry Trade Union, and a representative from the Business Trade Union. They submitted petitions to the Central Party Headquarters, the National Government, and the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, requesting three things: (1) to establish a permanent organization for trade unions; (2) to enact a separate law for trade unions; and (3) to revoke Notice No. 146 of the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau. The five representatives left for Nanjing on the night express last night.

Labor Dispute at French-owned Water and Electricity Company 205

Club Workers Destroy Union

At around 10:00 a.m. yesterday, the French-owned Electricity Company Vehicle Department Club, which has not been registered with party or government authorities, gathered a large number of people and stormed into the French-owned Water and Electricity Trade Union, destroying the equipment inside. At the time, the union members were at work, and only three or four clerks were in the office. As a result, Zheng Ruisheng was seriously injured. Rules for Handling Cases by the Municipal Chamber of Commerce 206

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, upon resolution by the Executive Committee, has stipulated the following eleven articles of the Rules for Handling Cases: (Article 1) These rules are formulated in accordance with the provisions of Chapter 2 of the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce Charter. (Article 2) The scope of cases handled by the Chamber shall be as follows: (1) Matters concerning the improvement and development of industrial and commercial enterprises; (2) Matters concerning industrial and commercial inquiries and notifications; (3) Matters concerning the introduction and guidance of international trade; (4) Matters concerning the investigation and compilation of industrial and commercial statistics; (5) Matters concerning industrial and commercial mediation and arbitration; (6) Matters concerning industrial and commercial certification and appraisal; (7) Matters concerning the handling of commodity collection and display; (8) Matters concerning the handling of commercial announcements; (9) Matters concerning the translation, verification, and commercial registration of Chinese and foreign documents entrusted by merchants; (10) Matters concerning commercial liquidation entrusted by parties or government authorities. (Article 3) The Chamber shall handle cases only when the applicant is currently a member of the Chamber, has paid the annual membership fee in accordance with the regulations, and the case falls within the scope of commercial affairs. (Article 4) Members of the Chamber who entrust the Chamber to handle the various items in Article 2 of these rules shall be entitled to free or reduced fees. (Article 5) If a non-member requests a case and the Chamber determines after review that it falls within the scope of commercial affairs, the Chamber may charge a reasonable handling fee to handle it. (Article 6) The handling fee charged by the Chamber shall be calculated at thirty yuan per case. (Article 7) If the case requested to be handled is too urgent, the handling fee stipulated above may be increased at the discretion of the Standing Committee of the Chamber. (Article 8) The handling fee for handling arbitration and liquidation matters shall be collected in accordance with the provisions of Article 20 of the Regulations of the Commercial Arbitration Office, jointly amended by the former Judicial and Agricultural-Commercial Ministry, which stipulates a fee of no more than two percent of the amount in dispute and is not subject to the restrictions of Article 6 of these rules. (Article 9) If the applicant is a member of the Chamber but the industry already has a trade association organization, they shall join the trade association in accordance with the law and request the association to handle it. (Article 10) Unless otherwise stipulated for the collection of fees, the Chamber shall handle all affairs in accordance with these rules. (Article 11) These rules shall be implemented upon resolution by the Executive Committee of the Chamber and shall be amended in the same way.

Shop Assistant Arrested for Secretly Collecting Customer Accounts 208

Yuan Haishan, a detective from the First District General Office of the Shanghai Special City Public Security Bureau, recently reported to the French Concession police that Xia Chenfa, the owner of Chengfeng Rice Store, reported that his shop assistant, Wang Yongchang, had secretly collected 1,800 yuan from customers. Rickshaw Puller on Wangjia Wharf 209

Conspires to Steal Luggage from Jiangyin Woman

Zhao Zhangshi, a thirty-three-year-old woman from Jiangyin, residing at No. 45 Zhoushan Lane, Tilanqiao, North Shanghai, returned to Shanghai by boat yesterday morning after traveling to her hometown. After disembarking at Wangjia Wharf in Nanshi, seven or eight rickshaw pullers rushed forward to solicit business. One of the rickshaw pullers, who did not have a concession license, persuaded her to hire him for 50 cents. After she got into the rickshaw, she turned around and found that her luggage, including her clothing box and bedding, was missing. She immediately searched for it but could not find it. Helpless, she reported it to Jin Jiushan, the security guard at the 15th post. After inquiring, it was learned that the rickshaw pullers had taken advantage of the woman being alone and surrounded her to bargain for the fare, taking the opportunity to steal her luggage. Chen Huifeng from Yancheng, one of the rickshaw pullers, was taken to the First Division of the First District by the police. After a preliminary interrogation by the station chief, he was charged with conspiring to steal the luggage of a passenger (commonly known as "knocking off the kerosene box"). He was ordered to prepare a document to be submitted to the Shanghai Public Security Bureau for investigation.

Qidong Bandit Flees to Shanghai Under Assumed Name 210

Is it Yuan Deren or Zhou Fuqing?

Chen Hualiang, secretly investigated by the Qidong County government, brought a document to the Third District Public Security Bureau of Pudong yesterday, stating that a bandit named Yuan Deren had committed crimes in the county and fled to Shanghai. It has been discovered that he is hiding in No. 63 Xiaoshi Bridge, Wujia Hall, Pudong, under the assumed name of Zhou Fuqing. He requested permission to send police to assist in arresting him and bringing him to justice. The district chief ordered the police to go with Chen to investigate. Yuan had left, so his wife, Zhang, was taken to the district for questioning. She confessed that she was twenty-three years old and that her husband had worked as a clerk in a paper mill in Jiaxing. Last October, they moved to Pudong and he changed his profession to doctor. He has been out for two days and has not returned. Ni Xiaogou is Worse Than a Beast 211

Uncle Sells Niece

Sister Accuses Brother

Ni Xiaogou, a peddler from Danyang, currently residing at No. 199 Luxiangyuan Road, Nine Mu Di, in the city, has an older sister, Li Ni, who lives in their hometown. She has a daughter, Li Xiaoyatou, who is eighteen years old. Last September, Ni Xiaogou returned to his hometown, and his sister entrusted her daughter to him to work in Shanghai, thinking that her uncle would take care of his niece. Unexpectedly, Ni Xiaogou, a beast in human clothing, saw that his niece was beautiful and sold Xiaoyatou to the Zhiji brothel in Dongxin Lane, Qianxin Street, for 360 yuan for a period of three years. After Ni got the money, he went to a casino and lost most of it. He spent the rest on prostitutes and is still a pauper without clothes. A year has passed, and his sister came to Shanghai to look for her daughter but could not find her. She learned that she had been sold and reported it to the detective team of the Municipal Public Security Bureau. Ni was arrested, and Li Xiaoyatou was also brought in. The case was transferred to the judicial department and then to the local court for trial yesterday.

Illegally Selling Lottery Tickets, Fined 2,000 Yuan 212

Li Yousheng, a detective from the gambling squad of the French Concession police, and Liu Kunbao, a patrolman, discovered that Zhang Yukuan, also known as Yang Yuquan, the owner of the Dayi Yuan Lottery Shop at No. 269 Edward Road, was illegally selling lottery tickets for the Yiyuan Dog Racing Track and the Shanghai Chinese Merchants Club. This was a violation of Article 281, Paragraph 2, of the Chinese Criminal Law and Article 75 of the Consular Instructions. On the 20th of this month, they went to the shop and confiscated several of these lottery tickets, which were taken to the police station. Yesterday, they were brought to the French court for trial. First, the Western detective explained the situation, and Zhang Yukuan admitted to illegally selling the tickets. The Chinese and Western judges ordered Zhang to be fined 2,000 yuan, the lottery tickets confiscated, and the case closed.

Local News Two

Strange Death of a Young Girl 215

Yu Azhi Dies

Zhou Dabang and Son Flee

At around 3 p.m. the day before yesterday, a young female corpse suddenly floated up in the Xiaohang Pond in front of the Nunnery in the West Market of Jiangwan, causing a sensation far and wide. Everyone was talking about it, but no one knew where the corpse came from. It was not until dusk that a woman named Yu Zhang came out to identify the body as her daughter. The details of the case are extremely strange, as the deceased is suspected of being murdered by her fiancé. The murderer has now fled. The details of this case are as follows:

Yu's Family Background: Yu Zhang, a woman residing in a northern house on Wan'an Road, Jiangwan, is originally from Wuxi. She is forty-three years old. Her husband, A San, is fifty-three years old. He used to be a groom at the Shanghai Racecourse but is now unemployed due to old age and weakness. They have two sons and two daughters. The eldest daughter, Xingmei, is already married. The second daughter, A Mao, is twenty-eight years old and beautiful. She is the murdered daughter. The two sons are Zhao Da, eleven years old, and a younger brother only five years old. Zhang makes a living by renting several acres of land for farming, which is enough to keep the family warm and fed.

A Mao's Child Betrothal: Yu Zhang's second daughter, A Mao, was promised in marriage to Zhou Yusheng, the youngest son of Zhou Dabang, a wealthy man in Dongtangjiaqiao, North Township, Jiangwan, through a matchmaker since she was a child. For the sake of saving expenses, A Mao was brought into the family as a child bride at the age of thirteen. However, Yusheng, who was nine years older than A Mao, had already had his first stirrings of love and wanted to take advantage of her, but he was unsuccessful because his fiancée was too young.

Forced Marriage Fails: Zhou Yusheng's father, Zhou Dabang, and his wife, Yan, had two sons, the eldest, Yinsheng, is thirty-one years old, and the second, Yusheng, is twenty-five years old. Both are workers in the Huafeng Yarn Factory, earning a meager living. Dabang longed for a grandson and wanted to marry his son as soon as possible, but he could not afford it due to economic constraints. He thought that his unmarried daughter-in-law was already in the house, so if they married early, he could avoid all the expenses. On the twenty-seventh day of the seventh lunar month, he forced A Mao to sleep with his son, but A Mao refused, resulting in her being scolded by her father-in-law. A Mao was extremely angry and fled to her mother's house that night, crying and telling her the whole story.

Sending the Daughter to Her Death: Although Yu Zhang hated Zhou Dabang's improper behavior, she feared that it would cause further trouble. The next morning, she accompanied her daughter back to Zhou's house and comforted her before returning home. However, two days later (the day before yesterday), on her way home from the fields, she heard people say that a woman had drowned in the Bingtang Pond, and that her appearance and clothes were similar to her daughter's. She went to see it out of curiosity and could not help but burst into tears. The corpse was indeed her daughter, A Mao.

Reporting to the Authorities: Yu Zhang believed that her daughter's death was strange, so she reported it to the Fifth Precinct, Fifth Station, claiming that her daughter had been mistreated by her father-in-law and had returned home. She had personally sent her back, but now she had suddenly died in the river, which was suspected to have been murdered by her father-in-law. She requested that the case be investigated. The station, considering the seriousness of the case, immediately ordered the patrolman to go to Dongtangjiaqiao to arrest the murderer, but Zhou Dabang and his son, Yusheng, had fled and could not be found. Zhou's wife, Yan, and her eldest son, Yinsheng, were arrested and interrogated, but they both claimed that they knew nothing. Yesterday morning, a document was prepared to send Zhou Yan and her son to the judicial department for further investigation. The police were also ordered to strictly arrest Zhou Dabang and Zhou Yusheng who are at large in order to get to the bottom of the matter.

Large Batch of Handguns Smuggled into Port 216

Japanese Police Station Investigating

The Shanghai Times reported that ten boxes of glassware arrived in Shanghai from Japan last Saturday. The customs declaration stated that they were all tanks, plates, vases, and glass ornaments. However, when the customs officer opened one of them and searched it slightly, he found five Mauser handguns. He immediately notified the police of the Japanese consulate, who detained the Japanese person who came to the customs to pick up the goods for investigation. Later, the remaining nine boxes were all opened and inspected, and it was found that each box contained ten handguns. Including the previous ones, a total of ninety-five handguns were seized. According to the Shanghai market price, each gun is worth more than 100 yuan, totaling nearly 10,000 yuan. The main people involved in the case are currently being investigated by the Japanese police in this port. It is also heard that the Japanese police authorities have arrested and are investigating the person who made the declaration based on a consultation from the Japanese consulate in this port.

Pirates Discovered in Xiaomiao Hongyang Waters Outside Wusong Port 217

Two Cargo Ships, Including Dasheng Factory Ships, Robbed by Pirates

The Empty Ship Recovered on the Beach by Warships

Gong Mianqin, the captain of the 17th team of the 4th district of the Wusong Waterborne Provincial Public Security Team, received a tip the night before last night around 9 p.m. that a large group of pirates aboard more than 20 pirate ships were robbing merchant ships in the Xiaomiao Hongyang waters outside Wusong Port. After receiving the report, Captain Gong immediately led a platoon of water police aboard the Pingyang warship and ordered Gong Yaozu, the captain of the Jinghai gunboat under his command, to proceed in separate directions. After searching for two hours, the two ships did not find any trace of the pirates. The Jinghai gunboat then sailed to the shallow beach on the Xigang waters and found two sailboats anchored there. Initially, they thought they were pirate ships and immediately inspected them, but they were empty ships with no one in charge. The two empty ships were then towed back to the team headquarters. After investigation, it was found that one of the ships was the No. 3 cargo ship of the No. 2 factory of Dasheng Yarn Factory, and the other belonged to Zhu Fuchang, a boatman there. Both ships had been robbed by pirates near Shangmiao Hong the day before yesterday. After confirming the facts, Captain Gong has already notified the shipowners separately to claim them yesterday and reported them to the district headquarters.

Uncle Abducts and Sells Niece 220

Sister, Thinking of Her Kin, Voluntarily Withdraws the Case

Crime Upon Crime, Unpardonable

Shen Bangchao, a forty-four-year-old man from Gaoyou, residing at No. 11, Zhilu, Youche Street, Nanshi, married a woman from the same hometown, Ji, as his wife and had a daughter named Qiaoyun, who is six years old. Ji's younger brother, Xinglou (thirty-six years old), is a rascal. On the twenty-ninth day of the seventh lunar month of this year, Xinglou actually lured his niece, Qiaoyun, to Pudong and sold her to someone surnamed Mou at Nanmatou to be a daughter, agreeing on a price of 20 yuan and falsely claiming that Qiaoyun was his own daughter. Because his wife had recently passed away and there was no one to take care of his young daughter, he sold her. Mou trusted him deeply. Unexpectedly, Qiaoyun was still childish and kept calling him uncle, which aroused Mou's suspicion. After repeated questioning, she finally told the truth. Mou was afraid of being implicated and immediately sent her to the Third Division of the Third District. After the station chief learned the truth, he sent police to Puxi to summon Qiaoyun's father, Shen Bangchao. Shen was out, so Ji went instead. After Xinglou repeatedly begged, Ji, thinking of their kinship, was unwilling to pursue the matter excessively, so the Third Division of the Third District sent a statement to the local court stating that Qiaoyun had been taken away by Xinglou and voluntarily withdrew the case. He was released yesterday. Unexpectedly, Bangchao has a cousin named Shen Fengzhu (thirty-five years old) who lives in the same house. His son, Hongxizi, nine years old, also disappeared on July 17th of this year. After searching everywhere without success, he heard of Xinglou's actions and suspected that he was also involved. After repeated strict investigation, they went to the house of someone surnamed Mou in Nanchujiaqiao, the French Concession, and found Hongxizi. At the same time, Xu Derong (fifty-three years old), an old man from Xinghua residing at No. 15 Youche Street, whose granddaughter had also disappeared the month before, also rushed to question him. Unexpectedly, Xinglou became angry and scolded Xu. Xu then called the police from the area to the First Division of the Third District. After a detailed interrogation by Station Chief Jin, he was charged with repeated kidnapping and immediately prepared a document to be sent to the court for verification.

Woman Harbouring a Kidnapping Victim Approved for Transfer to the Waterborne Public Security Team 221

Zhu Shen, a woman from Songjiang residing at No. 89, Santai Lane, North Shanxi Road, was previously found to have harboured a kidnapping victim. According to the investigation by members of the Waterborne Provincial Public Security Team, the facts are true. A request was sent to the Special District Local Court for assistance in the arrest. Yesterday morning, Judge Wu Tingqi interrogated her. The Waterborne Public Security Team did not send anyone to court, but Wang Yaotang, the lawyer for the police station, said that they would not object if she was transferred to the police station. Judge Wu then questioned Zhu Shen and ordered that the defendant be sent to the Jiangsu Waterborne Public Security Team for trial.

Huishi Police Station Arrests Bandits 222

The Huishi Police Station detective Bai Zhongqi discovered that bandits were hiding in the house at No. 2926, Yinhua Lane, Robert Road, Shanghai West. The day before yesterday, he led detectives Wang Debiao, Wu Shoushan, Liu Changgen, and others to the house to arrest them. Three men from Anhui, Li Dengxia, Ma Taiquan, and Zhang Songlin from Xuzhou, were found in the kitchen of the house, and two handguns and thirteen bullets were found under the bed. After further questioning, it was learned that there were still accomplices, Qian Jieshan, Yao Hongchang, and Qian Shaoshan from Jiangbei, hiding in two places at No. 1652 on the same road and No. 512 Haifang Road. They then went to those addresses and arrested the three men and brought them back to the police station. However, the details of the crimes committed needed to be further investigated. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Special District Local Court with a request to release Zhang and detain the others pending further investigation. After a brief interrogation of the defendants, Judge Wu approved the police station's request and ordered Zhang Songlin to be released on bail and the other five men, including Li Dengxia, to be taken back to the police station and detained for further questioning on October 3rd.
