Shao Xiao'di's Futile Search for His Wife 228

Zhao's Heart is Too Cruel

Shao Xiao'di, a 28-year-old villager from Changzhou, has always made a living farming in his hometown. His wife, Zhao, is currently 27 years old. They have been married for over six years and have one child each year, all of whom are young. The couple's feelings were originally very harmonious. However, since nearly two years ago, Shao has neglected farming and devoted himself to wandering and gambling, resulting in a difficult life for his elderly mother and several family members. Zhao repeatedly tried to persuade her husband, but to no avail. Zhao then changed her mind and suddenly abandoned her husband and children in the first month of this year, secretly fleeing. Shao searched everywhere but could not find any trace of her. Subsequently, Shao's children cried incessantly, his elderly mother became depressed and ill, and his livelihood was on the verge of collapse. He regretted his actions but it was too late. Confined to his home, he soon developed a mental disorder, with suicidal thoughts frequently expressed in his words. Now, he suddenly received a report from a fellow villager stating that his wife, Zhao, had become involved with someone in Shanghai and was working in a Japanese-owned yarn factory. Shao borrowed money from relatives and came to Shanghai alone this month. Initially, he temporarily resided with a friend in the French Concession's Xiaobeimen area. Later, after learning that his wife was living in the western part of Shanghai, he went to the Chen family's residence in Rongqingli, Laobaosheng Road, in western Shanghai on Sunday to stay temporarily. He waited and searched in front of various Japanese yarn factories every day. Unexpectedly, at around 6 p.m. the day before yesterday, Shao was wandering near the Xiaoshadu inside and outside yarn factories when he saw his wife leaving the factory. Shao immediately grabbed her, but she was not panicked. She spoke gently and told her husband not to pull and tug. Since they had met, she said it was best to talk things over. Shao then released her and asked her to return home with him. Zhao repeatedly agreed. It was already dark. As the two walked to the entrance of Yinghuali, Zhao said, "Wait here for a moment while I go inside to get a bag of clothes." Shao stood there for a long time but did not see her come out. Knowing that she had planned to escape, he went inside and saw rows of houses. He asked everywhere but could not find her. From then on, he was dejected and developed a desire to end his life. He immediately went to a deserted area near his friend's residence, untied his belt, and hanged himself from a bamboo fence. Fortunately, a resident of the area saw him, cried out in alarm, and people rescued him. He was lucky that it had not been long and he was revived. He was then escorted back to his friend Chen's residence.

Banning Shamans and Taibao 232

Order to Eliminate Superstition

The Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau issued an order to its district offices yesterday, stating: "The Municipal Party Department has sent a letter stating that the Ninth District Branch has requested the Municipal Public Security Bureau to effectively ban shamans and Taibao in order to eliminate superstition and maintain the lives of the people. The central government has already issued a clear order prohibiting shamans and Taibao, giving them three months to change their professions. However, these people believe that their days are numbered, so they make false claims, saying they can see ghosts and cure diseases, and draw talismans to prolong life, which causes foolish men and women to listen attentively. Some even seek help from shamans and Taibao for their children's illnesses instead of seeking medical treatment, and hope for talismans to prolong life instead of medicine and treatment. The result is that they die in vain and regret it endlessly. Therefore, in view of this, please request the bureau to effectively ban them in order to break superstition, etc. Upon approval, it is hereby ordered to strictly investigate and prohibit them, and not to procrastinate or neglect responsibilities."

Longan Import Permits are Uniformly One Year 237

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the Longan Trade Association yesterday, stating: "Regarding your inquiry as to whether the import permits for foreign goods such as dried longan will still be handled according to the previous regulations, we have inquired with the Jianghai Customs Superintendent. Last Year's Medical Report from Dehe Hospital 238

Hoping for Donations of Medicine Bottles, Old Clothes, and Toys

According to the 1929 report of Dehe Hospital (formerly Renji Hospital), the hospital treated 2,084 people injured on the road that year, of which 1,447 were hit by cars. In addition, it treated 771 people who fell, 15 people who took poison, 475 people who were injured by machines, 232 people who were crushed, 318 people who were burned, and 807 people who were injured in other accidents. According to the statistics compiled by the hospital, the number of men who committed suicide increased significantly, while the number of women who committed suicide decreased. The number of people who committed suicide by swallowing opium also decreased significantly. A total of 2,805 people were admitted to the hospital that year, including 1,994 men and 811 women and children. A total of 2,717 minor and serious illnesses were treated with medicine that year. The operating room was extremely busy, so the number of clothing staff and emergency service personnel was increased. A total of 2,654 X-rays were taken that year, 300 more than the previous year. The hospital spent a total of 70,000 yuan on the poor and sick that year. Most of these people suffered from acute illnesses and were sent by the patrol room, such as those injured by vehicles, suicides, bullet wounds, and beatings. The hospital is currently in need of empty medicine bottles, clean old clothes, toys, and other items needed by patients. It would be greatly appreciated if charitable people could donate to the hospital.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Urges Organization of Trade Associations 241

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday issued a notice to merchants in the city to organize trade associations in accordance with the law. The notice stated: "Article 7 of the amended Implementing Rules of the Chamber of Commerce Law stipulates that 'the term "trade without a trade association" refers to trades within the same region with fewer than seven businesses. When there are seven or more businesses, they may not join the Chamber of Commerce as businesses.' There are quite a few businesses in this city whose trades have seven or more businesses, but currently do not have a trade association. Their requests to join this Chamber of Commerce as business members cannot be accepted due to the restrictions of the regulations set by the Ministry. If this state of disunity continues, the common interests of the trades will inevitably not be guaranteed. In addition to this Chamber of Commerce sending personnel to investigate and urge them to organize trade associations, this notice is specially published to urge them to organize trade associations in accordance with the law and establish them within this year. If there are any ambiguities regarding the procedures for organizing a trade association, please go to the organization section of the commerce department of this Chamber of Commerce for guidance."

Notice of the Anti-Drug Propaganda Association 243

The anti-drug comrade associations organized by provinces, cities, and counties in the past have been reorganized into anti-drug propaganda associations by the Standing Committee of the Chinese National Anti-Drug Association in order to facilitate propaganda and easily control the propaganda associations. The organizational content of the propaganda associations is simple and not prone to abuse. There are strict regulations on the reorganization steps and the scope of work that the propaganda associations should do. In addition to conducting on-site propaganda for the anti-drug movement, they are not allowed to interfere in other matters. At the beginning of the reorganization of the propaganda associations, the seventh National Anti-Drug Movement Week is being held. The association is taking this opportunity to observe the efforts and achievements of the anti-drug propaganda associations in various places in order to identify those who should be retained and those who should be eliminated, and to award prizes accordingly. In addition to notifying them to make efforts to contact party and political organs and groups to prepare for the event on the spot, it issued another notice yesterday asking the anti-drug propaganda associations that are being reorganized to pay attention. The notice is extracted as follows: "Over the years, many anti-drug comrade associations in various places have been well-run, but there are also many that have achieved little. In order to seek a close-knit organization and make long-term considerations, this association has decided to reorganize all anti-drug comrade associations and branches that have not been formally approved into anti-drug propaganda associations. At the time of the preparation for the seventh Anti-Drug Movement Week, we will first start to sort out the preparations for the reorganization, and hereby notify all national anti-drug groups to hold Anti-Drug Movement Week from October 1 to 7 (delayed for one week in remote provinces) in accordance with the previously promulgated plan, focusing on anti-drug propaganda, and submit a report to this association one week after the event. This will be used as the standard for identifying those who should be retained and those who should be eliminated. If there are other reasons, please report them separately. This matter is of great importance to the future of anti-drug efforts, so please do not delay and hinder the progress. All fees paid previously will continue to be valid. We hereby attach this notice. We hope you will take note of it. Chinese National Anti-Drug Association."

Fire at Tiānzhāng Paper Mill in Pǔdōng 244

A fire broke out in the cloth room and machinery of the Tiānzhāng Paper Mill in Lùjiāzhái, Pǔdōng, at 1:10 PM yesterday. It was caused by a mechanic forgetting to add oil, which resulted in sparks igniting the cloth. Workers rushed to put out the fire, but it was already too intense and spread to the floorboards above. Workers upstairs panicked and fled down the ladder, but fortunately, they were not injured. The factory separately used telephones to alert the water and land authorities. Soon, a customs firefighting boat sailed to the factory's Bund, anchored, and connected a long hose to vigorously spray water into the burning room. It took about half an hour to extinguish the fire, but the floorboards were completely burned. Only the lead sheeting prevented objects from falling from above for the time being. Workers both upstairs and downstairs have temporarily stopped working.

County Reorganization Committee Members Cannot Concurrently Serve as District Chiefs 245

Other Concurrent Positions Must Also Be Submitted to the Province for Approval

The Shànghǎi County Reorganization Committee yesterday received a notice from the Jiāngsū Provincial Reorganization Committee stating: "In accordance with the decision made at the 61st meeting of this committee, county party committee members may not concurrently serve as district chiefs unless absolutely necessary. Any other concurrent positions must also be submitted to this committee for approval, and the office hours and whether or not they receive concurrent salaries for their current concurrent positions must be reported for record. Concurrent positions for staff members are absolutely prohibited. Those who already hold concurrent positions must resign and report immediately, in accordance with the instructions already issued to various counties in this committee's order No. 1251. The headquarters has now prepared a survey form for county party committee members and staff in Jiāngsū Province who hold concurrent positions, which is attached to this document. It is hoped that you will carefully fill it out in accordance with this committee's order No. 1251.

Impersonating Public Works Bureau Officials to Extort Money 248

Sentenced to Three Months in Prison

Yuè native Lǐ Yìmín falsely impersonated an official from the Public Works Bureau and suddenly went to the Xìnchéng Nánhuò Store at No. 440, Bàzǐ Road, on the first of this month. He claimed that the store's newly installed stove was too large and needed to be registered with the Public Works Bureau, otherwise it would be illegal and he would report it to the authorities. He then asked the store owner, Chén Yàotíng, for several hundred yuan to help him settle the matter. Chén refused and reported it to the Public Works Bureau. A foreigner told him that if he saw him again, he could report it to the nearest police station. Lǐ went to the store again the other day and said that a certain store on Wǔchāng Road had also asked him to find a way to settle the matter because of the large stove, and that it only cost 300 yuan. He said that if Chén continued to delay, he would inevitably be punished under Article 352 of the Criminal Code and the store would be sealed. At that time, Chén Yàotíng was out accounting, and Yú Qǐ, who came early, was informed by the store owner, so he was not fooled. He pretended to agree, and secretly sent someone to report to the police, who sent detectives to the store and arrested Lǐ. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the Special District Local Court for investigation. The police lawyer presented the forged letter written in Western language, which was found on the defendant. After questioning by Judge Féng, Lǐ was sentenced to three months in prison and the letter was confiscated.

Recent News from the Red Cross Epidemic Hospital 249

The Chinese Red Cross Society Epidemic Hospital was originally scheduled to close on the 20th of this month. Only doctors Wáng Zhènchuān, Zhōu Hóngzhāng, Zhāng Dānqīng, and pharmacist Yáng Shì and nurses Chén Qiūtáng and Gù Shìliáng remained to treat patients and wounded soldiers who had not been discharged from the hospital. It is said that committee member Lán Tíng intends to extend the work and keep the medical staff to continue to receive and treat acute epidemic diseases, and not to neglect human lives due to the closure.

Autumn Harvest in Shànghǎi County This Year 252

The autumn harvest in Shànghǎi County this year is generally considered abundant, but the cotton harvest is slightly poor. The county has a total of six districts: (1) Mǐnháng, (2) Tángwān, (3) Běiqiáo, (4) Sānlín, (5) Chénháng, and (6) Mǎqiáo. In the first district of Mǐnháng, heavy rain and hail in the previous month caused the cotton buds that had already formed to be completely destroyed. Therefore, they replanted three times, and the last time they encountered rain, most of the cotton buds that had bloomed were blown off. The cotton buds that had not bloomed were damp for too long, causing them to mold and rot. Although the other districts were not destroyed by hail, the yield per mu was only about 30 catties. In terms of rice, the first, third, fourth, fifth, and sixth districts have about 60% to 70% of the harvest, which is enough for the farmers to survive the winter. The second district, Tángwān, has a higher terrain and a better harvest than other villages.

Zhào Gēngyáng, a security guard at the 19th station of the First Section of the First District of the Shànghǎi Municipal Public Security Bureau, found a girl about four or five years old at Jīchǎng Street yesterday afternoon at around 6 PM. Special Feature

Li Yunliang Discusses Infringed Chinese Navigation Rights 258

The annual meeting of the Chinese Economic Society was held in the auditorium of the Wuxi County Chamber of Commerce at 9 AM on the day before yesterday (September 23rd). Mr. Li Yunliang, a local member with a master's degree, gave a public academic lecture on "Infringed Chinese Navigation Rights." Mr. Li has worked in the navigation industry for many years. This time, he elaborated in detail on the issue of Chinese navigation and the recovery of navigation rights. The following is a verbatim record of the speech by Mr. Xu Shishen from the Legislative Yuan.

Chairman, Ladies and Gentlemen: I am an economics student who has been working in the shipping industry for the past few years and have paid relatively close attention to the issues in the industry. I have benefited greatly from following the colleagues of the Economic Society to your area to tour. I take this opportunity to talk to you about the issue of navigation rights, which is related to the survival of the nation. I dare not call this an academic lecture. The topic I will be discussing today is "Infringed Chinese Navigation Rights," which I will divide into four sections. The first is the state of Chinese shipping under foreign powers' infringement. The second is the process of losing navigation rights. The third is the impact of the infringement. The fourth is the method of recovering navigation rights. Transportation is the lifeblood of a country, and railways and ships are the two major tools of transportation. However, even now, our country only has 8,000 miles of railways. On average, every 100 square miles accounts for one-sixth of a mile, and 400,000 people have only one mile of railways. Of course, this is not enough for application. Therefore, most of the transportation now still relies on shipping. The foundation of shipping lies in the coast and rivers. China's coastline, from Dadonggou at the mouth of the Yalu River on the border between China and Korea in the north, passes through Liaoning, Hebei, Shandong, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Fujian, and Guangdong to Beihai in the Gulf of Tonkin on the border between Guangdong and Saigon in southern Guangdong. It is a total of 13,000 miles. Compared with an area of ​​34.9 million square miles, every 2,600 square miles has only one mile of coastline. It is indeed very short. However, because the coastline is too short and there are relatively few harbors, we should pay special attention to protecting them. As for China's rivers, there are 12,000 miles that can be navigated by large ships and 34,000 miles that can be navigated by small ships, for a total of 46,000 miles. There are also 81,000 miles that can be navigated by civilian ships. Among them, the Yangtze River, Pearl River, and Heilongjiang River are the largest. In the north, the Heilongjiang River has 4,100 miles that can be navigated. In the south, the Pearl River has 1,800 miles that can be navigated. In the central area, the Yangtze River is one of the best rivers in the world and is China's treasure, with 4,900 miles navigable. There are also many tributaries, tens of thousands of miles, that can be navigated by small boats and civilian ships. Therefore, there are indeed many channels for China's shipping industry. However, over the years, due to the constraints of unequal treaties, navigation rights have been lost and foreigners have taken over. Now, foreign ships are even more developed than Chinese ships. China today has only 529 ships, totaling 400,000 tons. Calculated by population, each person only has two pounds and 1,000 people have only one ton. Taking a few of the most important companies as an example, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company has 25 ships, totaling 56,000 tons, operating on the Yangtze River, Ningbo, Wenzhou, Minjiang, North and South Pacific routes, and has a history of 56 years. The wharves in various places occupy important areas, but because there are too few ships, there has not been much progress over the years. On the contrary, it is under the control of foreign merchants. The second largest company is Sanbei, with 22 ships, totaling 35,000 tons, operating on the Yangtze River, Ningbo, and Minjiang routes. The third is Zhengji Company, with 22 ships, about 27,000 tons, which is the mainstay of coastal shipping. Most of the ships sail to Andong, Dalian, Qingdao, Shanghai, and Guangdong. The remaining larger ones include the Northeast Shipping Bureau, which is the only shipping agency in the Northeast, operating on the Songhua River and Yalu River, competing with Russia and Japan for navigation rights. However, Heihe is still controlled by the Russians. Zhaoxing Company originated in Yingkou, with 9 ships, operating in Yingkou, Dalian, Qingdao, Shanghai, and other places. Recently, it has also sent two or three ships to the Yangtze River and is acting as an agent for the shipping affairs of various small companies in the north. Ningshao Company has 4 ships operating in Ningbo and the Yangtze River and is a rising star. There are also many companies that are mostly less than 3,000 or 4,000 tons. Looking at the situation of China's shipping industry, although the number of ships is not small, most of the ships are too old (averaging 300-400 tons) and too old, so the coal consumption is high and the speed is slow, and they are not economical everywhere. Of course, it is not easy to compete. In recent years, due to military relations, the government often requisitions them, and they cannot operate normally, resulting in greater losses. Not only can they not progress, but they may not be able to maintain the status quo. Therefore, China's shipping industry is riddled with holes and is already on the verge of bankruptcy. Foreign ships operating on the Chinese coast, taking only the Taikoo, Jardine Matheson, Nissin, and Dalian four companies as examples, already have 161 ships totaling about 360,000 tons. Among them, the two British companies, Taikoo, account for 154,000 tons, and Jardine Matheson accounts for 98,000 tons. They occupy an advantageous position on the North and South Pacific and Yangtze River routes. The two Japanese companies, Nissin, have 50,000 tons and pay the most attention to the Yangtze River, and have ships sailing to Guangdong. Dalian, an affiliate of South Manchuria Railway, has 98,000 tons operating on Dalian, Qingdao, Tianjin, Shanghai, and other routes and is a strong force in the North Pacific. Recently, it has even expanded to the South Pacific and Hong Kong and Guangdong. The American-owned Jiangjiang Company specializes in sending shallow-water ships of less than 1,000 tons directly to Yichang and Chongqing, which is easy to operate and profitable and is a new force in the Yangtze River. Although I have not made detailed statistics of other companies, they probably total 200,000 tons. From this perspective, the power of foreign merchants is indeed more powerful than that of China's shipping industry. This year, there are about 70 million tons of ships in the world. The United Kingdom accounts for one-third, the United States accounts for one-fifth, and Japan accounts for one-twentieth. China's registered ships are only 320,000 tons, which is about four thousandths. Popularly scolding someone for being useless is "two hundred and five". Our country's shipping industry is less than "two hundred and five", only one two-hundred-and-fiftieth. It is obvious that China's shipping industry is controlled by the United Kingdom and Japan. Let's cite the customs statistics as proof. In the fifth year of Tongzhi (1864), there were a total of 6.6 million tons of shipping in and out throughout the year, and the United Kingdom actually accounted for half of it. Thirty years later, in the nineteenth year of Guangxu (1893), the tonnage of shipping increased to four and a half times, with 29 million tons. Foreign ships had 22,500 tons, and the United Kingdom accounted for 65% of the total, Japan 5%, and Chinese ships only 7 million tons, about 23%. More than 30 years later, last year, there were a total of 15,000 tons of ships in and out of the country. The British flag accounted for 37%, the Japanese flag accounted for 27%, and the Chinese flag only accounted for 23%. On average, there were 830 tons and 510 ships sailing every day, totaling 420,000 tons. Among them, the average foreign ship was 1,200 tons and there were 275 ships, totaling 340,000 tons. The average Chinese ship was 350 tons and there were 226 ships, totaling 80,000 tons. This is the general situation of Chinese and foreign shipping. Suzhou is not very developed in commerce. Among the 3,600 ships in and out of the customs last year, 900 were British and American ships, accounting for four-tenths of the total tonnage. Furthermore, in terms of inland port shipping, there are a total of 3,000 registered ships, but 550 of them fly foreign flags. Foreign ocean routes are completely controlled by foreign merchants. Except for the West Port and Hong Kong, our country does not have a single ton of shipping. From these many figures, it can be seen that China's shipping industry has been completely taken over by foreigners. Therefore, although the number of Chinese ships has gradually increased over the years, and on the surface it seems to have progressed, in reality it is just a painful history of the development of economic aggression by the powers on China's waters. The United Kingdom has a longer history of infringement and the greatest power. Japan is second, and other countries such as the United States, Norway, Germany, and France also have considerable power. They not only control our foreign ocean shipping, but also inland coastal, river, and port shipping has been infringed to the point of being incomplete. Everywhere, we only see the fluttering of foreign flags, coupled with the invasion of foreign warships into our country's territory, penetrating deep into the hinterland to show off their power. Anyone with blood would not be angry, if this can be tolerated, what cannot be tolerated? How could this phenomenon have been created? (To be continued)

The Political Program of the Chinese Kuomintang

Article 6 of the domestic policy: Determine that the people have complete freedom of assembly, association, speech, publication, residence, and belief.

Article 4 of the domestic policy: Implement universal suffrage and abolish class elections based on assets.

Article 7 and Article 8 of the domestic policy: Strictly determine the statutory amount of field tax and land tax, and prohibit all extra-legal levies, such as transit duties, which should be abolished.

Article 12 of the domestic policy: Recognize the principle of equality between men and women in law, economics, education, and society, and promote the development of women's rights. Article 9 of the domestic policy: Investigate household registration, reorganize arable land, and adjust the production and sales of grain to ensure that the people have enough food.

Youth Forum

Impressions of a Trip to the North (4) 259

— Su Ling

The South Manchuria Railway and the Chinese Eastern Railway

In the early morning, we boarded the South Manchuria train and continued northward.

The structure of the South Manchuria train is very beautiful. The third-class carriages can be compared with the second-class carriages of the Beijing-Shanghai train.

Looking out of the train window, the scenery is naturally that of the north. Snow-covered mountains and fields, clumps of gray empty forests, icy small rivers, and rows of short earthen houses with yellow smoke curling from their roofs... completely presenting a quiet and bleak atmosphere, much like an ancient beast left over from the Middle Ages, only sighing softly.

Especially the strangeness of those short earthen houses. The shape is like the carriages we are riding in, with slightly curved roofs, completely made of earth and mud, with very small window holes and smoke coming out of the roof because there is a heated kang inside. From these earthen houses, which are like Chinese-style coffins displayed one by one, we can imagine the simplicity of the lives of villagers in the Northeast.

The train passed through Fushun. From the train window, we could see a vague outline of this city outside the pass. It seemed that the houses were all the color of earthen red, and the entire city was filled with hazy yellow smoke.

At night, the train arrived in Changchun. Under the leadership of Mr. Chen, we stayed at an inn attached to the station. This inn is also very famous in Changchun, but inside it cannot make the travelers comfortable at all. Perhaps it is because I am not used to the life in the north. When you walk into the room, a large amount of water vapor gushes out, which will make you feel suffocated and difficult to breathe, as if you have walked into a public bathhouse.

We rested on a very large kang (?), which has been upgraded to not burn fire but use hot water pipes.

The people in this hotel are really too polite. From the tea boy to the handyman to the boss and manager (the northerners call them shopkeepers), and even the landlady, they all have to ask us how we are doing one by one, which really makes me overwhelmed. But I think this kind of hypocritical politeness only causes useless disturbance to the travelers.

The last leg of the journey from Changchun to Harbin was a solo trip for me.

The Chinese Eastern Railway train is obviously a contrast between a coarse and heavy one and a fine and small one. After the whistle made a piercing and strange cry, the heavy body of the train wriggled. In the cold night air, the train body seemed even heavier as it shook and rumbled, like a huge and elongated monster patrolling in the dark night.

As soon as I got on the train, I lay down and didn't know where the train had gone. I fell asleep, even though the train body was constantly shaking.

Returning Home 260

— Dai

From this experience of returning to my hometown, I am firmly convinced that my hometown is still in a desolate and miserable state.

I imagined that this separation of seven years might give my hometown an opportunity to improve. So when I came back from a faraway place, a bright scene was brilliantly presented and everything would be like the rising sun. But I was disappointed. On the uneven and rugged road, I gazed blankly around. There was no touching architecture, nor was there any fresh creation. I thought, is this the hometown after seven years of separation? Originally, from observing from the side, I had already understood that my hometown had not improved in any way.

The people are still the same people. I met many old relatives. They welcomed me warmly.

"How strange, oh, the guest from afar!" So I was surrounded by them. They asked me this and that, and I was almost overwhelmed. Naturally, a lot of excitement and fun were added to my lonely environment. However, I always found it a little annoying to be entangled by them. What's the use? This just shows that the people in my hometown are seeing something new.

Several gentlemen who were not very old were bare-armed and held water pipes in their hands, quietly listening to me talk. Sometimes they would add a sentence or two, but no matter what, their faces were always full of surprise and doubt. It seemed that they agreed and it seemed that they opposed.

"This has a fresh meaning, but our age is too high," they said, squeezing their beards. I didn't feel anything about this, but when I spoke, I did deliberately pay attention. Around me were several girls. They had never talked to a male of their age, or sat silently with a male. I carefully observed them. Although they were restrained from fear and shame by my serious and generous aura, they still occasionally showed an unsatisfactory attitude.

"Why don't they want to seize the freedom they deserve?" I asked.

They smiled at each other - "The reason is something I don't know."

In fact, it was also beyond my expectation. I still thought that this important commercial port on the coast would inevitably eliminate all the old-fashioned obstacles that were not conducive to relations between the two sexes after years of being shocked by the new trend. But it wasn't. They told me how strict the local etiquette was and how women could not have any upper-class rights to act. In the general view, establishing a proper friendship between the two sexes is the most impersonal and shameful thing.

I ran into a person's house. The owner was my brother-in-law. When I saw this house, I was shocked, because the dilapidated and declining scene after years of disrepair was suggesting future anxiety. There was no place that was more complete. It was broken and tilted. Five families lived in this small house. The living room was unlike anything. There were only two incomplete tables. The meals in the morning, noon and evening were inevitably taken in turns by each family. There were so many children, mostly one to four or five years old, naked and crying all day long, turning into a world of crying. The male owner was as thin as a stick. When he was a little upset, he would beat the child severely, and the crying would get louder and louder. The women were better, but a kind of exhausted expression showed that they had no spirit of revitalization.

This is a bleak world. The streets are as quiet as if they are asleep, except for a few cries from hawkers. The citizens of the whole county seem to be in a dream. They are dazed with their eyes. Although there is a strong stimulus, it is useless and they are still sleeping. The old people have passed away. They admit that they have reached the time of the tomb and there is no need to do any more troublesome work. The middle-aged people repeated the words of the old people and thought that they had not had enough cultivation in their youth and were just having a temporary good time. The teenagers only knew how to move around in the dark hell. They thought that the broad and healthy avenue that had been opened up in front of them was a place of snake venom and did not bother to move forward.

"Is there no one coming out to take responsibility for the transformation?" I asked my cousin.

"This is not a superficial problem," my cousin replied. "If you only observe the metaphysical depravity, it is easy to find a solution. But this strange society seems to have the poison flowing into everyone's flesh. The stubborn minds drive them to only seek safety in a simple life every day. They are willing to do so. Yes, after laziness penetrates, it is impossible to remedy. So when you use new theories to instill, the result is just inexplicable."

My cousin's words were right. I wandered in the sad streets for more than ten days, looking every day at the dilapidated houses and the confused crowds. They would shout

"Hey, guest from afar, how are you? Thanks to God, we are all well."

But the guest from afar sadly plucked his zither.

The morning sun goes west, to the sea

I reside here, wide and vast

Welcome, travellers on board

Disappointed, my hometown will never change

The spirit that falls into a deep dream declines

You barren hill has been through seven years

When I looked at you before, you still had vitality

Now silently, like an ancient corpse

Reader's Letter 261

Mr. Shouying

From the introduction in the Shenbao, I got to read your great work. I feel that your article "Night" is really beautifully written. What else can I do besides admire it?

Today, I am very presumptuous to ask the editor of the Shanghai Local Supplement of the Shenbao to forward this short letter to you. There is no other motive, I just want to be your friend. Would you agree?

You may have seen my name, but I hope you will show me your real name so that we can communicate. I wish you well.

Your brother Su Duyu, communicated on the 20th, at Lida Academy, Jiangwan.

(1) The content of the text should be related to youth issues, discussions on domestic and foreign schools or student news, essays, descriptions of school life, etc. The style is not limited.

(2) Books should be limited to those related to youth issues.

(5) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(6) Do not write horizontally and do not write in a messy manner. Western language should be omitted if possible. If it is necessary to quote the original text, it must be attached below the Chinese text.

Book and Newspaper Introductions

Nationalist Literary Criticism 263

— Tang Zengyang

Avant-Garde Weekly, Issues 11-13

Literary criticism has many varieties, because the objects of criticism differ in subject matter and method. For example, if the starting point of criticism is based on subject matter, dealing with historical facts is called historical criticism; dealing with various scientific or philosophical issues is called scientific criticism or philosophical criticism. Literary criticism (literary criticism) is naturally no exception to this scope, but it uses literature as the subject of criticism, that is to say, it uses literary works and issues as the object of criticism. Furthermore, if the goal of criticism is based on method, then criticism based on historical research methods is called historical criticism; criticism based on scientific principles and scientific research methods is called scientific criticism; criticism based on philosophical principles and research methods is naturally called philosophical criticism. Regarding this, the authors of Methods and Materials of Literary Criticism, Gayley and Scotts, once applied the perspective of criticism based on subject matter to literary works in the same way as mentioned above. In other words, criticism that uses literary works and issues as the object is called literary criticism (Literary criticism). But in terms of method, this "literary criticism" can be further divided into two types: judicial criticism and inductive criticism. In terms of schools of literary criticism, there are naturally many types. These schools of literary criticism arise with the schools of creation. Various methods of criticism, such as the so-called traditional criticism (Traditionlc

riticism) during the flourishing period of classicism (classicism), arose in response to these works. Other examples can be inferred based on this, without the need for further explanation. From this, it is sufficient to understand that criticism cannot be lacking when a certain kind of literature arises, and its importance in the literary category is of the same importance as other poetry or novels. Modern literary theorists say that literary criticism is also a kind of literary category. This statement has been established in European and American literary theories and is undoubtedly denied by literary foundations. In fact, literary criticism can also assist in the development of literary works. This involves the authors of literary criticism.

The prosperity of a nation's literature and art largely relies on the encouragement and guidance of literary critics. "The reason why Chinese literature and art have failed to embark on the correct path is certainly largely due to the lack of a correct central consciousness among literary authors, but at the same time, it is also an obvious fact that there are no literary critics who can grasp the correct central consciousness to guide them." From this perspective, literary critics are of utmost importance, especially in the Chinese literary world. Recently, amidst the surge of literary thought, our China has inevitably produced a kind of nationalist literature and art. In theory, it already has a definite foundation and is beyond doubt. However, during the gestation period of nationalist literary creation, nationalist literary critics must arise in response to creation. At the same time, there must be a correct assessment in critical judgments. Regarding this point, Mr. Xiang Hua's article "A Nationalist Literary Criticism" elaborates deep insights and establishes the judgments of literary critics. The new methods of nationalist literary creation can also be said to be the standards of nationalist literary criticism, which deserve special attention. The emergence of this article has a great influence on nationalist literary creation. Measuring the value of works according to this critical criterion can inevitably lead to outstanding progress in creations with a national center.

In "The Method of Nationalist Literary Criticism," the author explains the types of literary criticism produced in the past. By examining the essence of each type of literary criticism, the standards of its critical methods, and the roots of its diversity and disorder, it is clear that they mostly belong to the category of "mutual exclusion," and that no school of criticism has a perfect critical method, and that there is a lack of a central consciousness. Here, the author expresses a correct and precise judgment based on the results of his exploration: "What we need first is to be able to observe creation from the principles of nationalist literature and art. Furthermore, we must analyze whether the work is beneficial or harmful to the nation. At the same time, we must also consider the era and environment of the work, and pay attention to the perfection of its form and the richness of its content, and make a correct judgment that can never forget the standpoint of the group and be swayed by personal tastes, thereby repeating the mistakes of past individualistic literary criticism." This is the legal basis of nationalist literary criticism. Modern literary critics must base their estimates of the inherent value of nationalist literary creation on this principle in order to avoid all errors.

Before this methodology, the author examined "our current diverse and complex Chinese literary scene" with a precise eye. At the same time, he also explained that it is even more urgent to have literary critics with a correct central consciousness under such circumstances. During the period when nationalist literary creation is produced, just as Sainte-Beuve said, "A literary creator should have a literary critic to guide them." The same is true for nationalist literary creators. Secondly, the dissection of the Chinese people's lack of a spirit of criticism and their erroneous concepts is even more incisive and can be regarded as an extremely brilliant conclusion, for example:

Originally, the Chinese have always lacked a spirit of criticism, so all progress has been exceptionally slow. In literature, criticism is especially not valued. If we trace the remains of criticism in literary history, all we find is the general singing of "literature carries the Way" by corrupt scholars, or the mixing of Taoist thought and the playing of "spirit" and "qi." So it can be simply said that China has never had literary critics; those who exist are nothing more than executioners who harm literature and art.

This is such a shameful thing. Originally, the term "literary criticism" has only been gradually mentioned with the budding of new literature in recent years. As for the various guiding responsibilities of critics, whether they have been fulfilled and what the results of their efforts are, we are silent about it, but the author of this article also has detailed explanations and criticisms. As for the section "The Purpose of Nationalist Literary Criticism," it is also based on the outline of "The Purpose of a Literary Criticism" mentioned in "Methods and Materials of Literary Criticism" co-authored by Scott and Gayley, and it gives rise to "The Purpose of Nationalist Literary Criticism," which has nine points, that is, the critical criteria of literary criticism, which are worth noting.

Finally, the explanation of "The Current Task of Nationalist Literary Criticism" is extremely important. The author's argument is based on "The Purpose of Literary Criticism":

The current task of nationalist literature and art must never forget the national democratic spirit, absolutely support the literary creation of the general public, develop the nation's upward will, eliminate all thoughts that hinder national progress, and express the history of national struggle. In nationalist literary criticism, he must grasp his critical method, recognize his purpose and mission, and conduct a rigorous analysis and judgment of literary works. All works of feudal thought, decadent thought, and otherworldly thought, as well as those that wave the flag for Soviet Russia, harbor conspiracies to destroy the Chinese nation, and pro-labor works that seek to undermine national consciousness with class consciousness, should be eradicated with all their strength. At the same time, works that are in line with the purpose and mission of our nationalist literary criticism must be vigorously promoted, especially for new works and new writers, they should be supported with all their strength, guiding them with a correct central consciousness and guiding them to develop in this direction.

This is indeed a clear determination of "the current task of nationalist literary criticism," which no one can deny. In short, in the present day of constructing nationalist literary creation, such a non-empty grand theory from the author is urgently needed.

Submission Guidelines for Book and Newspaper Introductions 264

(1) The text is limited to introducing the latest domestic and foreign publications. In addition to literary works, all political, economic, legal, scientific, educational, etc. books and newspapers are included in the introduction. However, boring books and newspapers will not be introduced.

(2) The paintings are limited to new works by new domestic and foreign artists and attached illustrations related to the text.

Market News 265

Since its opening at the new location at the intersection of Third Ma Road and Stone Road, Da Xin Silk and Satin Bureau has been doing very well. In addition, various new-style silk crepes are sold vigorously because the prices are low and the patterns are original. The shop assistants are especially attentive in their service, it is said.

They have long been praised by all walks of life. Therefore, every Mid-Autumn Festival, customers are crowded and often in short supply. In order to thank our patrons, we have specially hired many famous Cantonese pastry chefs to carefully craft them with richer materials than before, in order to improve quality and keep prices low. We would be very grateful for your patronage, it is said.

All wholesale purchases within the month will still be given preferential treatment at the original price.

In order to give preferential treatment to our patrons, we are selling a kind of preferential voucher, each card is one yuan, each book is twelve cards, totaling twelve yuan, now sold for ten yuan, so buyers are very enthusiastic, it is said.
